    96	
    97	def _values_equal(got: Any, want: Any, tol: float = 1e-9) -> bool:
    98	    if isinstance(got, bool) != isinstance(want, bool):
    99	        return False
   100	    # LLM workers answer in text: "3767" must satisfy an expected 3767
   101	    if isinstance(want, (int, float)) and isinstance(got, str):
   102	        try:
   103	            got = float(got.strip().rstrip("."))
   104	        except ValueError:  # non-numeric answer text; float(str) never raises OverflowError (→ inf)
   105	            return False
   106	    if isinstance(got, (int, float)) and isinstance(want, (int, float)):
   107	        try:
   108	            return math.isclose(float(got), float(want), rel_tol=tol, abs_tol=tol)
   109	        except OverflowError:  # a huge numeric got/want/one_of member → non-match, never a crash
   110	            return False
   111	    if isinstance(got, str) and isinstance(want, str):
   112	        return got.strip() == want.strip()  # LLM answers carry incidental whitespace
   113	    return got == want
   114	
   115	
   116	def verify_output(task: Task, result: WorkerResult) -> VerificationResult:
   117	    """Deterministic verdict for one attempt. FAIL always carries a reason; a
   118	    missing ground-truth signal yields UNVERIFIED, never a fake PASS.
   119	
   120	    UNVERIFIED is the least-bad verdict for malformed ground truth: it avoids
   121	    deterministic false-blame and matrix FAIL recording (gate.py:100 only records
   122	    PASS/FAIL), but it is NOT fully neutral — the optimization loop still counts
   123	    non-PASS as a miss (loop.py:125). (codex P2.)"""
   124	    if result.error:
   125	        if result.error.startswith("schema:"):
   126	            mode = MASTMode.SCHEMA_INVALID
   127	        elif result.timed_out:                      # issue #2
   128	            mode = MASTMode.TIMEOUT
   129	        else:
   130	            mode = MASTMode.TOOL_ERROR
   131	        return VerificationResult(
   132	            verdict=Verdict.FAIL, score=0.0, detail=result.error, failure_mode=mode,
   133	            scorer="execution",
   134	        )
   135	
   136	    if task.output_schema:
   137	        try:
   138	            Draft202012Validator.check_schema(task.output_schema)
   139	            schema_errors = sorted(
   140	                Draft202012Validator(task.output_schema).iter_errors(result.output),
   141	                key=lambda error: tuple(str(part) for part in error.absolute_path),
   142	            )
   143	        except SchemaError as exc:
   144	            return VerificationResult(
   145	                verdict=Verdict.UNVERIFIED,
   146	                score=0.5,
   147	                detail=f"invalid output schema: {exc.message}",
   148	                scorer="none",
   149	            )
   150	        if schema_errors:
   151	            return VerificationResult(
   152	                verdict=Verdict.FAIL,
   153	                score=0.0,
   154	                detail="; ".join(error.message for error in schema_errors),
   155	                failure_mode=MASTMode.SCHEMA_INVALID,
   156	                scorer="schema",
   157	            )
   158	
   159	    check = task.success_check
   160	    if not check:
   161	        return VerificationResult(
   162	            verdict=Verdict.UNVERIFIED, score=0.5,
   163	            detail="no checkable success signal for this task", scorer="none",
   164	        )
   165	
   166	    # Malformed collection/string checks must never become tautologies.  In
   167	    # particular, membership in a string iterates characters and every string
   168	    # contains ""; both previously allowed malformed ground truth to PASS.
   169	    if "contains" in check and (
   170	        not isinstance(check["contains"], str) or not check["contains"].strip()
   171	    ):
   172	        return VerificationResult(
   173	            verdict=Verdict.UNVERIFIED,
   174	            score=0.5,
   175	            detail="success_check contains must be a nonempty string",
   176	            scorer="none",
   177	        )
   178	    if "one_of" in check and (
   179	        not isinstance(check["one_of"], list) or not check["one_of"]
   180	    ):
    55	    requires_execution_evidence: bool = False
    56	    # conditional execution: {"step": "<id>", "equals"|"contains"|"one_of": value,
    57	    # "negate": bool} — evaluated deterministically against the referenced step's
    58	    # output at advance-time; unmet -> this step is journaled as skipped
    59	    when: Optional[dict[str, Any]] = None
    60	
    61	    @model_validator(mode="after")
    62	    def _assignment_is_unambiguous(self) -> "StepSpec":
    63	        self.role = (self.role.strip() or None) if self.role else None
    64	        self.worker_id = (self.worker_id.strip() or None) if self.worker_id else None
    65	        self.required_capabilities = list(dict.fromkeys(
    66	            value.strip() for value in self.required_capabilities if value.strip()
    67	        ))
    68	        if self.worker_id and self.tier_hint is not None:
    69	            raise ValueError("worker_id and tier_hint cannot be combined")
    70	        return self
    71	
    72	    def to_task(
    73	        self,
    74	        resolved_inputs: dict[str, Any],
    75	        *,
    76	        objective: str | None = None,
    77	        boundaries: list[str] | None = None,
    78	    ) -> Task:
    79	        boundaries = list(self.boundaries if boundaries is None else boundaries)
    80	        # a one_of check is a format contract the worker deserves to see spelled
    81	        # out — exact-match verification punishes prose around a right answer
    82	        if self.success_check and "one_of" in self.success_check:
    83	            allowed = ", ".join(repr(v) for v in self.success_check["one_of"])
    84	            boundaries.append(
    85	                f"Respond with exactly one of the following values and nothing else: {allowed}."
    86	            )
    87	        return Task(
    88	            task_type=self.task_type,
    89	            objective=self.objective if objective is None else objective,
    90	            inputs=resolved_inputs,
    91	            output_schema=self.output_schema,
    92	            boundaries=boundaries,
    93	            success_check=self.success_check,
    94	            tier_hint=self.tier_hint,
    95	            role=self.role,
    96	            required_capabilities=list(self.required_capabilities),
    97	            worker_id=self.worker_id,
    98	            max_attempts=self.max_attempts,
    99	            tools=list(self.tools),
   100	            requires_execution_evidence=self.requires_execution_evidence,
   101	        )
   102

   191	        with tracer().start_as_current_span("enrich.self_critique") as span:
   192	            span.set_attribute("task.id", task.id)
   193	            result = await self.inner.run(task)
   194	            if result.error:
   195	                return result
   196	            extra_in = extra_out = 0
   197	            extra_cost = extra_latency = 0.0

   200	                critique_task = Task(
   201	                    task_type=TaskType.REASONING,

   213	                    **task.inputs,
   214	                    "previous_draft": result.raw_text or str(result.output),
   215	                    "reviewer_critique": critique_text,
   216	                }

   219	                    "'previous_draft') and found the issues listed in "
   220	                    "'reviewer_critique'. Produce an improved answer that fixes "
   221	                    "those issues while still satisfying the original objective.",
   222	                ]
   223	                revised = await self.inner.run(revise_task)
   224	                extra_in += revised.tokens_in; extra_out += revised.tokens_out
   225	                extra_cost += revised.cost_usd; extra_latency += revised.latency_s
   226	                if revised.error:
   227	                    break
   228	                revised.task_id = task.id
   229	                result = revised
   230	                rounds_used += 1
   231	            result.tokens_in += extra_in
   232	            result.tokens_out += extra_out
   233	            result.cost_usd += extra_cost
   234	            result.latency_s += extra_latency
   235	            span.set_attribute("enrich.critique_rounds", rounds_used)
   236	            return self._resign(result)

   203	    def append_event(
   204	        self,
   205	        kind: str,
   206	        run_id: str,
   207	        step_id: Optional[str] = None,
   208	        payload: Optional[dict[str, Any]] = None,
   209	        *,
   210	        snapshot_digest: Optional[str] = None,
   211	        attempt_id: Optional[str] = None,
   212	    ) -> RunEvent | JournalEntry | None:
   213	        if not self._canonical:
   214	            # A resumed historical stream stays historical; never mix formats.
   215	            # Events with no old equivalent are intentionally absent there.
   216	            projected_kind: Optional[str]
   217	            projected_payload = dict(payload or {})
   218	            if kind in {"run.started", "step.started"}:
   219	                projected_kind = kind
   220	            elif kind == "verification.completed":
   221	                projected_kind = "step.attempt"
   222	            elif kind == "approval.required":
   223	                projected_kind = "hitl.requested"
   224	            elif kind == "approval.resolved":
   225	                projected_kind = "hitl.resolved"
   226	            elif kind in {"step.completed", "step.failed", "step.skipped"}:
   227	                projected_kind = kind
   228	            elif kind in {"run.completed", "run.failed"}:
   229	                projected_kind = "run.finished"
   230	                projected_payload.setdefault(
   231	                    "status", "completed" if kind == "run.completed" else "failed"
   232	                )
   233	            else:
   234	                projected_kind = None
   235	            if projected_kind is None:
   236	                return None
   237	            return self.append(
   238	                projected_kind, run_id, step_id=step_id, payload=projected_payload
   239	            )
   240	        with self.transaction(refresh=self._lock_fd is None):
   241	            digest = snapshot_digest or self._snapshot_digest
   242	            if digest is None:
   243	                raise ValueError("canonical events require a snapshot digest")
   244	            if self._run_id is not None and run_id != self._run_id:
   245	                raise ValueError(
   246	                    f"journal is bound to run {self._run_id!r}, not {run_id!r}"
   247	                )
   248	            if self._snapshot_digest is not None and digest != self._snapshot_digest:
   249	                raise ValueError("snapshot digest changed within journal")
   250	            event = RunEvent(
   251	                seq=len(self._records), at=time.time(), kind=kind,
   252	                run_id=run_id, snapshot_digest=digest, step_id=step_id,
   253	                attempt_id=attempt_id, payload=payload or {},
   254	            )
   255	            if event.seq == 0 and event.kind != "run.started":
   256	                raise ValueError("canonical journal must begin with run.started")
   257	            if event.seq > 0 and event.kind == "run.started":
   258	                raise ValueError("canonical journal may contain only one run.started")
   259	            _validate_canonical_history([
   260	                *[item for item in self._records if isinstance(item, RunEvent)],
   261	                event,
   262	            ])
   263	            self._write_record(event)
   264	            self._records.append(event)
   265	            self._run_id = run_id
   266	            self._snapshot_digest = digest
   267	            return event
   268	
   269	    def append(
   270	        self,
   271	        kind: str,
   272	        run_id: str,
   273	        step_id: Optional[str] = None,
   274	        payload: Optional[dict[str, Any]] = None,
   275	    ) -> JournalEntry:
   276	        """Append a historical-format record (compatibility fixtures only)."""
   277	        if self._canonical:
   278	            raise ValueError("canonical journals require append_event")
   279	        with self.transaction(refresh=self._lock_fd is None):
   280	            if self._run_id is not None and run_id != self._run_id:
   281	                raise ValueError(
   282	                    f"journal is bound to run {self._run_id!r}, not {run_id!r}"
   283	                )
   284	            entry = JournalEntry(
   285	                seq=len(self._records), at=time.time(), kind=kind,
   286	                run_id=run_id, step_id=step_id, payload=payload or {},
   287	            )
   288	            self._write_record(entry)
   289	            self._records.append(entry)
   290	            self._run_id = run_id
   291	            return entry
   292	
   293	    def events(self, kind: Optional[str] = None) -> list[RunEvent | JournalEntry]:
   294	        records = list(self._records)
   295	        if kind is not None:
   296	            records = [event for event in records if event.kind == kind]
   297	        return records
   298	
   299	    def entries(self, kind: Optional[str] = None) -> list[JournalEntry]:
   300	        if self._canonical:
   301	            projected = [
   302	                entry for event in self._records
   303	                if isinstance(event, RunEvent)
   304	                for entry in [_legacy_projection(event)] if entry is not None
   305	            ]
   306	            # Legacy consumers expect their own contiguous sequence, not gaps
   307	            # created by canonical events that have no historical equivalent.
   308	            projected = [entry.model_copy(update={"seq": seq})
   309	                         for seq, entry in enumerate(projected)]
   310	        else:
   311	            projected = [entry for entry in self._records
   312	                         if isinstance(entry, JournalEntry)]
   313	        if kind is not None:
   314	            projected = [entry for entry in projected if entry.kind == kind]
   315	        return projected

    32	    engine = WorkflowEngine(_executor(), journal_dir=tmp_path)
    33	    run = engine.start(_spec())
    34	    run = await engine.advance(run.run_id)
    35	    journal = engine.journal(run.run_id)
    36	
    37	    events = journal.events()

    43	        "run.started", "step.ready", "step.started", "attempt.assigned",
    44	        "attempt.started", "verification.started", "verification.completed",

    52	        "requested_capabilities": [], "requested_worker_id": None,
    53	    }

    56	                 for line in (tmp_path / f"{run.run_id}.jsonl").read_text().splitlines()]

    58	    assert "step.attempt" not in raw_kinds
    59	    assert "run.finished" not in raw_kinds

    61	        "run.started", "step.started", "step.attempt", "step.completed",
    62	        "run.finished",

    66	async def test_approval_resolution_is_idempotent_and_opposite_conflicts(tmp_path):
    67	    engine = WorkflowEngine(_executor(), journal_dir=tmp_path)

   121	async def test_two_resumed_engines_run_completed_step_at_most_once(tmp_path):
   122	    calls = 0
   123	
   124	    class SlowExecutor:
   125	        async def execute(self, task: Task, *, event_sink=None) -> TaskOutcome:
   126	            nonlocal calls
   127	            calls += 1
   128	            await asyncio.sleep(0.05)
   129	            return TaskOutcome(
   130	                task=task, final_verdict=Verdict.PASS, final_output="ok"
   131	            )
   132	
   133	    first = WorkflowEngine(SlowExecutor(), journal_dir=tmp_path)
   134	    run = first.start(_spec())
   135	    path = tmp_path / f"{run.run_id}.jsonl"
   136	    left, _ = WorkflowEngine.resume(path, SlowExecutor())
   137	    right, _ = WorkflowEngine.resume(path, SlowExecutor())
   138	
   139	    left_state, right_state = await asyncio.gather(
   140	        left.advance(run.run_id), right.advance(run.run_id)
   141	    )
   142	    assert calls == 1
   143	    assert left_state.status is RunStatus.COMPLETED
   144	    assert right_state.status is RunStatus.COMPLETED
   145	    loaded = Journal.load(path)
   146	    assert len(loaded.events("step.completed")) == 1
   147	    assert len(loaded.events("run.completed")) == 1
   148

   320	    def _lock_path(self) -> Path:
   321	        assert self._path is not None
   322	        return self._path.with_name(self._path.name + ".lock")
   323	
   324	    def acquire(self, *, refresh: bool = True) -> None:
   325	        if self._path is None or self._lock_fd is not None:
   326	            return
   327	        self._path.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
   328	        flags = os.O_RDWR | os.O_CREAT
   329	        if hasattr(os, "O_CLOEXEC"):
   330	            flags |= os.O_CLOEXEC
   331	        if hasattr(os, "O_NOFOLLOW"):
   332	            flags |= os.O_NOFOLLOW
   333	        fd = os.open(self._lock_path(), flags, 0o600)
   334	        if not stat.S_ISREG(os.fstat(fd).st_mode):
   335	            os.close(fd)
   336	            raise ValueError("journal lock path is not a regular file")
   337	        fcntl.flock(fd, fcntl.LOCK_EX)
   338	        self._lock_fd = fd
   339	        try:
   340	            if refresh and self._path.exists():
   341	                self._load_into_self()
   342	        except Exception:
   343	            self.release()
   344	            raise
   345	
   346	    def release(self) -> None:
   347	        if self._lock_fd is None:
   348	            return
   349	        fd, self._lock_fd = self._lock_fd, None
   350	        try:
   351	            fcntl.flock(fd, fcntl.LOCK_UN)
   352	        finally:
   353	            os.close(fd)
   354	
   355	    @contextlib.contextmanager
   356	    def transaction(self, *, refresh: bool = True) -> Iterator["Journal"]:
   357	        owned = self._lock_fd is None
   358	        if owned:
   359	            self.acquire(refresh=refresh)
   360	        try:
   361	            yield self
   362	        finally:
   363	            if owned:
   364	                self.release()
   365	
   366	    def _write_record(self, record: RunEvent | JournalEntry) -> None:
   367	        if self._path is None:
   368	            return
   369	        self._path.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
   370	        existed = self._path.exists()
   371	        flags = os.O_WRONLY | os.O_APPEND | os.O_CREAT
   372	        if hasattr(os, "O_CLOEXEC"):
   373	            flags |= os.O_CLOEXEC
   374	        if hasattr(os, "O_NOFOLLOW"):
   375	            flags |= os.O_NOFOLLOW
   376	        fd = os.open(self._path, flags, 0o600)
   377	        try:
   378	            if not stat.S_ISREG(os.fstat(fd).st_mode):
   379	                raise ValueError("journal path is not a regular file")
   380	            data = (json.dumps(
   381	                record.model_dump(mode="json"), sort_keys=True,
   382	                ensure_ascii=False, allow_nan=False,
   383	            ) + "\n").encode("utf-8")
   384	            view = memoryview(data)
   385	            while view:
   386	                written = os.write(fd, view)
   387	                if written <= 0:
   388	                    raise OSError("short write appending journal")
   389	                view = view[written:]
   390	            os.fsync(fd)
   391	        finally:
   392	            os.close(fd)
   393	        if not existed:
   394	            dir_fd = os.open(self._path.parent, os.O_RDONLY)
   395	            try:
   396	                os.fsync(dir_fd)
   397	            finally:
   398	                os.close(dir_fd)

   400	    @classmethod
   401	    def load(cls, path: str | Path) -> "Journal":
   402	        journal = cls(path=path)
   403	        # Readers take the same sidecar lock as writers, so they never mistake
   404	        # an append in progress for a truncated/corrupt terminal record.
   405	        with journal.transaction(refresh=True):
   406	            pass
   407	        return journal
   408	
   409	    def _load_into_self(self) -> None:
   410	        assert self._path is not None
   411	        try:
   412	            st = self._path.lstat()
   413	        except FileNotFoundError:
   414	            self._records = []
   415	            self._run_id = None
   416	            self._snapshot_digest = None
   417	            return
   418	        if stat.S_ISLNK(st.st_mode) or not stat.S_ISREG(st.st_mode):
   419	            raise ValueError("journal path must be a regular non-symlink file")
   420	        raw = self._path.read_bytes()
   421	        if raw and not raw.endswith(b"\n"):
   422	            raise ValueError("journal has a truncated final record")
   423	        try:
   424	            text = raw.decode("utf-8")
   425	        except UnicodeDecodeError as exc:
   426	            raise ValueError("journal is not valid UTF-8") from exc
   427	        parsed = [_parse_line(line, line_no=n)
   428	                  for n, line in enumerate(text.splitlines(), 1)]
   429	        if not parsed:
   430	            self._records = []
   431	            self._run_id = None
   432	            self._snapshot_digest = None
   433	            return
   434	        canonical_flags = ["schema_version" in value for value in parsed]
   435	        if any(canonical_flags) and not all(canonical_flags):
   436	            raise ValueError("journal mixes canonical and legacy records")
   437	        canonical = all(canonical_flags)
   438	        records: list[RunEvent | JournalEntry] = []
   439	        for expected_seq, value in enumerate(parsed):

   441	            try:
   442	                record = model.model_validate(value)

   444	                raise ValueError(

   449	                    f"journal sequence gap at line {expected_seq + 1}: "
   450	                    f"expected {expected_seq}, got {record.seq}"
   451	                )
   452	            records.append(record)
   453	        run_ids = {record.run_id for record in records}
   454	        if len(run_ids) != 1:
   455	            raise ValueError("journal contains mixed run IDs")

   148	def _validate_canonical_history(events: list[RunEvent]) -> None:
   149	    if not events:
   150	        return
   151	    if events[0].kind != "run.started":
   152	        raise ValueError("canonical journal must begin with run.started")
   153	    if sum(event.kind == "run.started" for event in events) != 1:
   154	        raise ValueError("canonical journal must contain one run.started")
   155	    terminals = [event for event in events if event.kind in {"run.completed", "run.failed"}]
   156	    if len(terminals) > 1:
   157	        raise ValueError("canonical journal has duplicate run terminal events")
   158	    if terminals and events[-1] is not terminals[0]:
   159	        raise ValueError("canonical journal has events after its run terminal")
   160	    step_terminals: set[str] = set()
   161	    for event in events:
   162	        if event.kind in {"step.completed", "step.failed", "step.skipped"}:
   163	            assert event.step_id is not None
   164	            if event.step_id in step_terminals:
   165	                raise ValueError(
   166	                    f"canonical journal has duplicate terminal for step {event.step_id!r}"
   167	                )
   168	            step_terminals.add(event.step_id)

   171	class Journal:
   172	    """A strict durable journal with a legacy compatibility mode.
   173	
   174	    Engine-created journals are canonical.  Direct callers using ``append``
   175	    keep the historical shape, which is useful for archived fixtures.  A file
   176	    may never mix the two formats.
   177	    """
   178	
   179	    def __init__(self, path: Optional[str | Path] = None, *, canonical: bool = False) -> None:
   180	        self._records: list[RunEvent | JournalEntry] = []
   181	        self._path = Path(path) if path else None
   182	        self._canonical = canonical
   183	        self._run_id: Optional[str] = None
   184	        self._snapshot_digest: Optional[str] = None
   185	        self._lock_fd: Optional[int] = None
   186	
   187	    @property
   188	    def is_canonical(self) -> bool:
   189	        return self._canonical
   190	
   191	    def initialize(
   192	        self, run_id: str, payload: dict[str, Any], *, snapshot_digest: str
   193	    ) -> RunEvent:
   194	        """Create canonical seq-0 ``run.started`` and bind stream identity."""
   195	        if not self._canonical:
   196	            raise ValueError("initialize is only valid for canonical journals")
   197	        if self._records:
   198	            raise ValueError("journal is already initialized")
   199	        return self.append_event(
   200	            "run.started", run_id, payload=payload, snapshot_digest=snapshot_digest
   201	        )
   202	
   203	    def append_event(
   450	                    f"expected {expected_seq}, got {record.seq}"
   451	                )
   452	            records.append(record)
   453	        run_ids = {record.run_id for record in records}
   454	        if len(run_ids) != 1:
   455	            raise ValueError("journal contains mixed run IDs")
   456	        self._canonical = canonical
   457	        self._records = records
   458	        self._run_id = records[0].run_id
   459	        if canonical:
   460	            events = [event for event in records if isinstance(event, RunEvent)]
   461	            _validate_canonical_history(events)
   462	            digests = {event.snapshot_digest for event in events}
   463	            if len(digests) != 1:
   464	                raise ValueError("snapshot digest changed within journal")
   465	            digest = events[0].snapshot_digest
   466	            payload_digest = events[0].payload.get("snapshot_digest")
   467	            if payload_digest is not None and payload_digest != digest:
   468	                raise ValueError("run.started payload snapshot digest mismatch")
   469	            self._snapshot_digest = digest
   470	        else:
   471	            self._snapshot_digest = None

    78	      sections, then the `ContextEnvelope` and `ContextManifest` exactly as

    80	      `_make_envelope`, hashing). Messages = rendered from sections; the

# Verdict: UNSOUND

The shared-assembler direction is reasonable, but the current staged design cannot satisfy the journal, live-redaction, or trust-enforcement acceptance boxes within its owned paths. Several failures would remain invisible to the proposed tests.

1. **P0 — `context.manifest` cannot reach the durable journal.**

   The attempt sink binding is real: `TaskExecutor` adds `n` and binds the worker hook at [executor.py:210](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/core/executor.py:210). `WorkflowEngine` forwards the emitted kind directly into `Journal.append_event()` at [engine.py:444](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/workflows/engine.py:444).

   However, `RunEvent` only permits the kinds listed at [journal.py:22](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/workflows/journal.py:22), and rejects anything else at [journal.py:55](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/workflows/journal.py:55). `context.manifest` is absent. I confirmed directly that constructing that event raises `ValidationError: unknown canonical event kind 'context.manifest'`.

   Because worker telemetry exceptions are swallowed at [local.py:235](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/local.py:235), real workflow execution would continue while silently losing every manifest. Legacy journals also discard unprojectable kinds at [journal.py:213](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/workflows/journal.py:213).

   **Fix:** Expand ownership to `workflows/journal.py` and its tests. Add `context.manifest` as an attempt-scoped canonical kind, require `attempt_id`, define legacy-resume behavior, and add an end-to-end `WorkflowEngine → TaskExecutor → worker → Journal.load()` test. A direct bound-sink unit test is not evidence of journaling.

2. **P0 — Treating every boundary as `RESPONSE_CONTRACT/INSTRUCTION` launders generated and untrusted material.**

   Original task boundaries are an instruction contract, as documented at [types.py:87](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/core/types.py:87). But `TaskExecutor` appends heterogeneous `advice` into the same list at [executor.py:97](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/core/executor.py:97). That advice includes:

   - Retrieved selflearn blocks returned at [adapter.py:84](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/knowledge/adapter.py:84).
   - Prior worker output embedded verbatim by the reflector at [reflexion.py:66](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/correction/reflexion.py:66).
   - Verifier or execution details interpolated at [reflexion.py:29](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/correction/reflexion.py:29) and [reflexion.py:49](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/correction/reflexion.py:49).

   Stage 2 would declare all of this `INSTRUCTION`, so the assembler’s trust check would approve the caller’s false declaration. The proposed negative test proves only that the assembler rejects an explicitly untrusted draft; it does not prove the real caller assigns trust correctly.

   **Fix:** Preserve provenance before `TaskExecutor` merges these values. Keep original task boundaries and authorized `PromptDirectives` as `RESPONSE_CONTRACT/INSTRUCTION`; render retrieved hints, prior outputs, and diagnostics in non-instruction sections such as `MEMORY`, `PRIOR_OUTPUTS`, or `VERIFIER_FEEDBACK` with `GENERATED_SUMMARY`/`UNTRUSTED_EVIDENCE`. This requires expanding scope beyond the currently owned files.

3. **P0 — Redaction and “what the model saw” do not cover all transmitted surfaces.**

   Local requests send tool schemas separately from messages at [local.py:149](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/local.py:149) and [local.py:250](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/local.py:250). The proposed `LiveAssembly` returns no redacted `tool_schemas`, so `_body()` would still receive the original schemas even if the manifest contains redacted copies.

   Coding has two more discrepancies:

   - Pi and Claude put raw `worker.system_prompt` into argv at [coding.py:93](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/coding.py:93) and [coding.py:126](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/coding.py:126), bypassing assembly redaction.
   - Codex and OpenCode do not pass `system_prompt` at all, as shown by their builders at [coding.py:99](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/coding.py:99) and [coding.py:111](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/coding.py:111). A manifest claiming those models saw it would be false.

   `ContextManifestEntry.surface` only supports `"message"` and `"tool_schemas"` at [models.py:309](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/context/models.py:309); it cannot attest a flat stdin/argv prompt or append-system-prompt surface.

   **Fix:** Make `LiveAssembly` return every fitted/redacted transport value: messages, tool schemas, flat prompt, and system prompt. Adapters must consume those returned values, never `self.system_prompt` or the original schemas. Add explicit manifest surfaces/reconstruction for flat prompt and system-prompt transport, which means revising the supposedly frozen model contract. For adapters lacking a system flag, either inject the redacted system text into the prompt or omit it truthfully.

4. **P1 — `SectionDraft` cannot preserve assistant tool-call messages.**

   The live transcript requires the assistant message’s structured `tool_calls` array at [local.py:273](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/local.py:273), followed by tool responses referencing `tool_call_id` at [local.py:287](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/local.py:287).

   The proposed draft contains only string content, role, and `tool_call_id`. Reconstructing the second round would therefore drop `tool_calls`, producing an invalid or semantically incomplete chat transcript.

   **Fix:** Add typed structured message metadata, particularly `tool_calls`, to the draft/rendering model. Redact it recursively, include it in manifest hashes, and test the exact second-round request body—not merely that a permissive fake endpoint was called twice.

5. **P1 — Section receipts and manifest entries lack a defined one-to-one contract.**

   The manifest requires exactly one compression receipt per entry, in the same stable-ID order, at [models.py:358](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/context/models.py:358). Entries represent rendered messages or schema arrays at [models.py:309](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/context/models.py:309), while the spec calls for receipts per declared section.

   Local currently combines several logical sections into one system message and one user message at [local.py:43](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/local.py:43). Coding combines all non-system sections into one flat prompt at [coding.py:273](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/coding.py:273). The spec does not say whether entries are per draft, per final message, or per transport surface. Coalescing breaks per-section alignment; emitting one message per section changes prompt behavior; omitted sections make the ambiguity worse.

   Envelope construction also requires unique stable IDs and exactly contiguous priorities at [models.py:236](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/context/models.py:236).

   **Fix:** Define grouping and receipt granularity before implementation. Prefer separate section-level receipts and transport-surface entries in the model, with an explicit section-to-surface mapping. Add validator tests for coalesced messages, omitted drafts, tool schemas, and coding’s flat prompt.

6. **P1 — Fail-closed assembly is correct, but downstream semantics turn contract failures into model failures and retries.**

   Removing the legacy fallback is appropriate for security. The availability problem is downstream: `BaseRunner` converts every assembler exception into a normal `WorkerResult.error` at [runner.py:122](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/runner.py:122). Verification then classifies it as `TOOL_ERROR` at [verifiers.py:124](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/evals/verifiers.py:124).

   The executor can record that as negative model capability evidence at [executor.py:377](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/core/executor.py:377), reflect, and retry/escalate at [executor.py:426](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/core/executor.py:426). A deterministic context-contract defect could therefore waste every attempt and poison routing evidence.

   **Fix:** Keep fail-closed behavior, but introduce an explicit non-model `CONTEXT_CONTRACT` failure classification. Abort retries for deterministic assembly violations and exclude them from capability learning. This requires executor/verifier scope or a pre-routing validation boundary; do not restore legacy rendering.

7. **P1 — Existing head/tail compression is not a hard budget fitter.**

   `allocate_section_budgets()` may assign zero-token allocations at [assembly.py:86](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/context/assembly.py:86). `digest_text()` always adds a pruning marker at [registry.py:67](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/tools/registry.py:67), so even `digest_text(text, 0)` produces six estimated tokens. Existing tests explicitly accept compression growth at [test_context.py:182](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/tests/test_context.py:182).

   `ContextSection` does not require compressed tokens to fit `budget_tokens`, and permits compressed output to exceed original size for non-`NONE` actions at [models.py:207](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/context/models.py:207). Protected sections also cannot be omitted at [models.py:220](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/context/models.py:220).

   **Fix:** Add a postcondition over the actual returned messages, schemas, and CLI surfaces. If protected content cannot fit, raise a typed pre-call violation. Define deterministic behavior for zero/tiny allocations instead of assuming `digest_text` satisfies them.

8. **P2 — Hidden inheritance and test couplings are understated.**

   There are no additional direct production callers of `_build_messages`, `_render_prompt`, or `fit_messages_with_receipt`; that narrow call-graph claim is correct. However:

   - `SubscriptionWorker` inherits `CodingAgentWorker` at [subscription.py:65](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/subscription.py:65), so every Stage 3 behavior change also affects subscription/read-only workers.
   - Adapter behavior differs across all four CLIs at [coding.py:88](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/coding.py:88); one stub-binary test is insufficient.
   - The necessary durable-journal integration belongs in `tests/test_run_events.py`, which is outside the owned test list.
   - Shadow-specific tests continue beyond the cited region, including fallback at [test_context.py:334](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/tests/test_context.py:334) and tool-round manifests at [test_context.py:366](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/tests/test_context.py:366).
   - Preserving `fit_messages` and `fit_messages_with_receipt` unchanged is necessary: `tests/test_tools.py` still consumes the former at [test_tools.py:125](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/tests/test_tools.py:125), and several adversarial suites exercise the latter.

   **Fix:** Add subscription coverage, parameterize coding tests over all adapters, include real journal integration tests, and enumerate every superseded shadow test explicitly.

A smaller validator conflict should also be resolved or documented: `evidence_snapshot_version` is non-nullable at [models.py:103](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/context/models.py:103), while the breaking-version validator requires it to be `None` at [models.py:111](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/context/models.py:111). A generic live API accepting arbitrary version bindings will encounter that dead-end.

No files were changed; the worktree was clean at base `46c60fad04eb92f07d33b5c02f00e2fd9f30413f`.

# Verdict: UNSOUND

The shared-assembler direction is reasonable, but the current staged design cannot satisfy the journal, live-redaction, or trust-enforcement acceptance boxes within its owned paths. Several failures would remain invisible to the proposed tests.

1. **P0 — `context.manifest` cannot reach the durable journal.**

   The attempt sink binding is real: `TaskExecutor` adds `n` and binds the worker hook at [executor.py:210](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/core/executor.py:210). `WorkflowEngine` forwards the emitted kind directly into `Journal.append_event()` at [engine.py:444](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/workflows/engine.py:444).

   However, `RunEvent` only permits the kinds listed at [journal.py:22](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/workflows/journal.py:22), and rejects anything else at [journal.py:55](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/workflows/journal.py:55). `context.manifest` is absent. I confirmed directly that constructing that event raises `ValidationError: unknown canonical event kind 'context.manifest'`.

   Because worker telemetry exceptions are swallowed at [local.py:235](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/local.py:235), real workflow execution would continue while silently losing every manifest. Legacy journals also discard unprojectable kinds at [journal.py:213](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/workflows/journal.py:213).

   **Fix:** Expand ownership to `workflows/journal.py` and its tests. Add `context.manifest` as an attempt-scoped canonical kind, require `attempt_id`, define legacy-resume behavior, and add an end-to-end `WorkflowEngine → TaskExecutor → worker → Journal.load()` test. A direct bound-sink unit test is not evidence of journaling.

2. **P0 — Treating every boundary as `RESPONSE_CONTRACT/INSTRUCTION` launders generated and untrusted material.**

   Original task boundaries are an instruction contract, as documented at [types.py:87](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/core/types.py:87). But `TaskExecutor` appends heterogeneous `advice` into the same list at [executor.py:97](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/core/executor.py:97). That advice includes:

   - Retrieved selflearn blocks returned at [adapter.py:84](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/knowledge/adapter.py:84).
   - Prior worker output embedded verbatim by the reflector at [reflexion.py:66](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/correction/reflexion.py:66).
   - Verifier or execution details interpolated at [reflexion.py:29](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/correction/reflexion.py:29) and [reflexion.py:49](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/correction/reflexion.py:49).

   Stage 2 would declare all of this `INSTRUCTION`, so the assembler’s trust check would approve the caller’s false declaration. The proposed negative test proves only that the assembler rejects an explicitly untrusted draft; it does not prove the real caller assigns trust correctly.

   **Fix:** Preserve provenance before `TaskExecutor` merges these values. Keep original task boundaries and authorized `PromptDirectives` as `RESPONSE_CONTRACT/INSTRUCTION`; render retrieved hints, prior outputs, and diagnostics in non-instruction sections such as `MEMORY`, `PRIOR_OUTPUTS`, or `VERIFIER_FEEDBACK` with `GENERATED_SUMMARY`/`UNTRUSTED_EVIDENCE`. This requires expanding scope beyond the currently owned files.

3. **P0 — Redaction and “what the model saw” do not cover all transmitted surfaces.**

   Local requests send tool schemas separately from messages at [local.py:149](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/local.py:149) and [local.py:250](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/local.py:250). The proposed `LiveAssembly` returns no redacted `tool_schemas`, so `_body()` would still receive the original schemas even if the manifest contains redacted copies.

   Coding has two more discrepancies:

   - Pi and Claude put raw `worker.system_prompt` into argv at [coding.py:93](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/coding.py:93) and [coding.py:126](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/coding.py:126), bypassing assembly redaction.
   - Codex and OpenCode do not pass `system_prompt` at all, as shown by their builders at [coding.py:99](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/coding.py:99) and [coding.py:111](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/coding.py:111). A manifest claiming those models saw it would be false.

   `ContextManifestEntry.surface` only supports `"message"` and `"tool_schemas"` at [models.py:309](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/context/models.py:309); it cannot attest a flat stdin/argv prompt or append-system-prompt surface.

   **Fix:** Make `LiveAssembly` return every fitted/redacted transport value: messages, tool schemas, flat prompt, and system prompt. Adapters must consume those returned values, never `self.system_prompt` or the original schemas. Add explicit manifest surfaces/reconstruction for flat prompt and system-prompt transport, which means revising the supposedly frozen model contract. For adapters lacking a system flag, either inject the redacted system text into the prompt or omit it truthfully.

4. **P1 — `SectionDraft` cannot preserve assistant tool-call messages.**

   The live transcript requires the assistant message’s structured `tool_calls` array at [local.py:273](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/local.py:273), followed by tool responses referencing `tool_call_id` at [local.py:287](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/local.py:287).

   The proposed draft contains only string content, role, and `tool_call_id`. Reconstructing the second round would therefore drop `tool_calls`, producing an invalid or semantically incomplete chat transcript.

   **Fix:** Add typed structured message metadata, particularly `tool_calls`, to the draft/rendering model. Redact it recursively, include it in manifest hashes, and test the exact second-round request body—not merely that a permissive fake endpoint was called twice.

5. **P1 — Section receipts and manifest entries lack a defined one-to-one contract.**

   The manifest requires exactly one compression receipt per entry, in the same stable-ID order, at [models.py:358](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/context/models.py:358). Entries represent rendered messages or schema arrays at [models.py:309](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/context/models.py:309), while the spec calls for receipts per declared section.

   Local currently combines several logical sections into one system message and one user message at [local.py:43](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/local.py:43). Coding combines all non-system sections into one flat prompt at [coding.py:273](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/coding.py:273). The spec does not say whether entries are per draft, per final message, or per transport surface. Coalescing breaks per-section alignment; emitting one message per section changes prompt behavior; omitted sections make the ambiguity worse.

   Envelope construction also requires unique stable IDs and exactly contiguous priorities at [models.py:236](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/context/models.py:236).

   **Fix:** Define grouping and receipt granularity before implementation. Prefer separate section-level receipts and transport-surface entries in the model, with an explicit section-to-surface mapping. Add validator tests for coalesced messages, omitted drafts, tool schemas, and coding’s flat prompt.

6. **P1 — Fail-closed assembly is correct, but downstream semantics turn contract failures into model failures and retries.**

   Removing the legacy fallback is appropriate for security. The availability problem is downstream: `BaseRunner` converts every assembler exception into a normal `WorkerResult.error` at [runner.py:122](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/runner.py:122). Verification then classifies it as `TOOL_ERROR` at [verifiers.py:124](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/evals/verifiers.py:124).

   The executor can record that as negative model capability evidence at [executor.py:377](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/core/executor.py:377), reflect, and retry/escalate at [executor.py:426](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/core/executor.py:426). A deterministic context-contract defect could therefore waste every attempt and poison routing evidence.

   **Fix:** Keep fail-closed behavior, but introduce an explicit non-model `CONTEXT_CONTRACT` failure classification. Abort retries for deterministic assembly violations and exclude them from capability learning. This requires executor/verifier scope or a pre-routing validation boundary; do not restore legacy rendering.

7. **P1 — Existing head/tail compression is not a hard budget fitter.**

   `allocate_section_budgets()` may assign zero-token allocations at [assembly.py:86](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/context/assembly.py:86). `digest_text()` always adds a pruning marker at [registry.py:67](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/tools/registry.py:67), so even `digest_text(text, 0)` produces six estimated tokens. Existing tests explicitly accept compression growth at [test_context.py:182](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/tests/test_context.py:182).

   `ContextSection` does not require compressed tokens to fit `budget_tokens`, and permits compressed output to exceed original size for non-`NONE` actions at [models.py:207](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/context/models.py:207). Protected sections also cannot be omitted at [models.py:220](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/context/models.py:220).

   **Fix:** Add a postcondition over the actual returned messages, schemas, and CLI surfaces. If protected content cannot fit, raise a typed pre-call violation. Define deterministic behavior for zero/tiny allocations instead of assuming `digest_text` satisfies them.

8. **P2 — Hidden inheritance and test couplings are understated.**

   There are no additional direct production callers of `_build_messages`, `_render_prompt`, or `fit_messages_with_receipt`; that narrow call-graph claim is correct. However:

   - `SubscriptionWorker` inherits `CodingAgentWorker` at [subscription.py:65](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/subscription.py:65), so every Stage 3 behavior change also affects subscription/read-only workers.
   - Adapter behavior differs across all four CLIs at [coding.py:88](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/harness/coding.py:88); one stub-binary test is insufficient.
   - The necessary durable-journal integration belongs in `tests/test_run_events.py`, which is outside the owned test list.
   - Shadow-specific tests continue beyond the cited region, including fallback at [test_context.py:334](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/tests/test_context.py:334) and tool-round manifests at [test_context.py:366](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/tests/test_context.py:366).
   - Preserving `fit_messages` and `fit_messages_with_receipt` unchanged is necessary: `tests/test_tools.py` still consumes the former at [test_tools.py:125](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/tests/test_tools.py:125), and several adversarial suites exercise the latter.

   **Fix:** Add subscription coverage, parameterize coding tests over all adapters, include real journal integration tests, and enumerate every superseded shadow test explicitly.

A smaller validator conflict should also be resolved or documented: `evidence_snapshot_version` is non-nullable at [models.py:103](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/context/models.py:103), while the breaking-version validator requires it to be `None` at [models.py:111](/private/tmp/meta-harness-meta-19/src/metaharness/context/models.py:111). A generic live API accepting arbitrary version bindings will encounter that dead-end.

No files were changed; the worktree was clean at base `46c60fad04eb92f07d33b5c02f00e2fd9f30413f`.
